### Post by koleoptero on 2010-08-31
It's September somewhere already.

Rules:

1. Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
2. If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
3. Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
4. The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
5. The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
6. Please use reduced-size thumbnails, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
7. To avoid having users having to ask you for them. when possible we request that you format your posts in the following order: NOTE this is optional

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

**Important Note:** Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.


Here it goes:

GTK: Modified version of jurialmunkey's [Victorious Elements]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=9683935&postcount=208").
Metacity: The one included in the Absolute gtk theme (gnome-look.org)
Icons: Faenza Cupertino (gnome-look.org)
Wallpaper: [clicky]("http://dl.dropbox.com/u/1612038/1-9-10/2005-05-29-1920x1200.jpg")
Font: Segoe UI semibold size 9
Dock is AWN with custom theme.

[[IMG]http://dl.dropbox.com/u/1612038/1-9-10/Screenshot-th.png[/IMG]]("http://dl.dropbox.com/u/1612038/1-9-10/Screenshot.png")

[[IMG]http://dl.dropbox.com/u/1612038/1-9-10/Screenshot-1-th.png[/IMG]]("http://dl.dropbox.com/u/1612038/1-9-10/Screenshot-1.png")

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-08-31
> **koleoptero said:**
> Now you just posted this equinox version of your theme to make mine feel outdated, didn't you? :P

Hahaha. Perhaps just a little. I wanted to re-write everything from scratch using only the equinox engine. The old one was put together in a scrappy fashion from elementary, WOW and victory GTKs. I'm still not entirely happy with the scrollbars, and I don't think I'm going to get them where I want them without using pixmaps. Also, I'm not sure how to fix the hinting (the faint blue selection outline) on entry-boxes to include the drop-arrow - it looks weird because only three sides of the entry box will have hinting and the arrow on the right side wont.



### EDIT ###
I gave up and submitted to using pixmap scrollbars. Thanks to lassekongo83's "Cold Snap" gtk for the scrollbars. I also made an equinox version of lassekongo83's "droid" emerald theme. 

[Download Victorious-Equinox V2]("http://ubuntuone.com/p/EY7/")
(Put emerald in ~/.emerald/themes/ && Theme in /usr/share/themes/)

[IMG]http://i73.photobucket.com/albums/i202/jurialmunkey/Screenshot-51resized.jpg[/IMG]

---

### Post by TheVerySpecialAgent on 2010-09-01
> **TyrantWave said:**
> How'd you apply that filter? I'd love that :drool:

In the new version there is a code view, there you can apply whatever filter you want.

I have attached a file with my icon settings, import it in the acyl gui, go the the codeview, refresh to check if it works, apply. ;)

The filter does not scale well to all icon sizes, especially the small ones, an example of this is the rhythmbox icon in the top right corner of my screenshot. I suspect it is because of svg rendering problems in gnome.

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-09-01
> **desnaike said:**
> Be more specific about the problems you see.

The GTK theme looks like redmond or whatever gnome defaults to when the selected theme can't be loaded. It has happened to me a lot of times while tinkering themes. It has also happened to me with some murrine-based themes that needed the newest one while I had some older one.

Try installing this: [http://rghost.net/2427728](http://rghost.net/2427728)

Unless that gtk theme looks as it is supposed to look which means I'm a jerk and you're ok.

### Post by arzali on 2010-09-04
> **Dekrus said:**
> How do you have the b6pre? I downloaded the tar.gz2 and no way to get it working...

Also, do a tutorial to make it like that.

im Using a "portable" version of firefox. i just downloaded firefox-4.0b6pre.en-US.linux-i686.tar.bz2, extracted into the firefox-portable folder, dubble click on "loader.sh" and choose execute thats all. i uploaded my portable firefox with including stylish styles for elementary and ambiance.

the best thing with the loader.sh is you can run the betas at the same time with your current installed version of firefox

[http://dl.dropbox.com/u/2137781/Firefox-Portable.tar.gz](http://dl.dropbox.com/u/2137781/Firefox-Portable.tar.gz)

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-09-05
> **danielrmt said:**
> Whats your Metacity/Emerald/WM theme?

Its a modification of droid by lassekongo: [linky]("http://lassekongo83.deviantart.com/art/droid-174374235?q=&qo=")

My mod is bundled with my GTK here: [linky]("http://ubuntuone.com/p/EY7/")

Theres a .tar inside, and inside that is a folder. In that folder is "Themes" and "Emerald". Put the contents of themes in /usr/share/ (you need sudo) and the contents of emerald in ~/.emerald/themes/

EDIT:: Oh yeah, you need the equinox gtk engine! :D

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-09-07
GTK: jurialmunkey's Victorious equinox with custom soothing dark-blue highlights (look earlier in this thread)
Metacity: Equinox Evolution ( sudo add-apt-repository ppa:tiheum/equinox && sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get install equinox-* )
Icons: Faenza (should be installed with the previous step)
Prorams: Dock is awn floaty with custom theme, elementary nautilus, deadbeef.
Music: [Clicky]("http://www.jamendo.com/en/album/28378")

[[IMG]http://dl.dropbox.com/u/1612038/7-9-10/Screenshot-th.png[/IMG]]("http://dl.dropbox.com/u/1612038/7-9-10/Screenshot.png")

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-09-07
> **koleoptero said:**
> Now I need to do something with xcompmgr to get shadows under the windows and menus cause they all blend too much.
Dark backdrops usually do well with heavy shadows.
 try 'xcompmgr -cfF -t-7.9 -l-8 -r5.6 -o.55 -D1' (play with o and D values for shadow weight and fade time)

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-09-10
@the8thstar
Pardon my ignorance (I don't have Burg... or Gnome... or Ubuntu for that matter), but does the use of Burg mean that you can have an image of your choice from grub right until a usable desktop and beyond (without any blanking out or flickering in between), regardless of DE or WM?

If that's true, then I might give it a go. Wonder how easy it is to get working on other distros.....

---

### Post by the8thstar on 2010-09-10
@gutterslob:

Short answer: no.

Reasoning:

You still need a few steps to get your desktop going:

0. Push the power button and see bios splash
1. Grub / Burg
2. Plymouth
3. GDM Login Screen
4. Desktop

Through steps 1, 2 and 3 the screen flickers. Between 3 and 4, it doesn't. Tweaking Burg and the GDM to end up with a similar background as the desktop is easy, but  tweaking plymouth to get the same result is beyond the reach of mere mortals.

---

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-09-10
> **Half-Left said:**
> For those who wanted my GNOME Shell theme, you can download it here [http://half-left.deviantart.com/#/d2yfxag](http://half-left.deviantart.com/#/d2yfxag) 
*snip*
Enjoy. :)

Thanks! Wow... very beautiful. 

One thing though. When I first installed it, I was getting heaps of corruption on my window decorations. I realised it was a problem with file permissions... This is what I had to do to fix it
In a terminal:
```
cd /usr/share/gnome-shell
sudo chmod 777 theme
sudo chmod 777 theme/*
```

closed all windows
restarted gnome-shell

Then it worked fine. Really beautiful work though!

---

### Post by teh'p3nsi0n3r on 2010-09-11
> **robbiemacg said:**
> Can you share some of the particulars, please?

sure, i followed this guide for the dock/icons. Read the comments below. watch out for step 4. follow some of the advise for step from the comments below. - i used ubuntu tweak to edit my panels under the session section. change "gnome-panel" to "avant-window-navigator". Easily reset back that way. Thats why to avoid step 4 because whats suggested in the article, folk have screwed up there panels and cannot revert back.

[http://www.omgubuntu.co.uk/2010/09/how-to-fully-replace-your-gnome-panels-with-awn/](http://www.omgubuntu.co.uk/2010/09/how-to-fully-replace-your-gnome-panels-with-awn/)

os - pinguyOS - already has nautilus-elementary & conky already configured.
dock - awn
wallpaper - "wooden wallpaper" search on deviant art, there are plenty.
icons - AwOken
Equinox Ambience window border - from gnome-look
window controls - Ambience - already in Ubuntu 10.04.

hope this helps.

---

### Post by Ransoms on 2010-09-11
> **skrite said:**
> really dig your conky clock, mind posting the conkyrc?

Sure, here it is..

```
background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=16
xftalpha 0.1
update_interval 1
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 280 200
maximum_width 320
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
default_color d2d2d2
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white
alignment top_left
gap_x 22
gap_y 0
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale no
TEXT

${goto 30}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=96}${time %H}${voffset -48}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:bold:size=38}${time :%M}${voffset -18}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:bold:size=18}${time %S}       

${goto 150}${voffset -10}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=18}${time %A}      
${goto 150}${voffset -4}${time %d %B %Y}  

$membar

${voffset -14}Uptime:$alignr$uptime
RAM:$alignr$mem/$memmax
Swap usage:$alignr$swap/$swapmax
Disk usage:$alignr${fs_used /}/${fs_size /}
Processor 1:$alignr${cpu cpu1}%
Processor 2:$alignr${cpu cpu2}%
```

---

### Post by finny388 on 2010-09-12
> **jodlajodla said:**
> Hey!
How can I configurate DockBarX, to get only icons in panel? (Did I need to only install it?)
How much using of RAM and processor does it need? Did I need normal effects? 
I have 3.20 GHz dual processor (Intel), 1GB RAM, and integrated graphics 128MB RAM. 

I have 1 more question: How can I change Ubuntu menu like Win XP/7? 
How much using of RAM and processor does it need?

Thanks for anwsers! :)

**DockbarX**
Yes, you need only to install it. Once you install you won't see it until you add it to panel. It will appear Add to Panel when you right-click the panel and choose "Add to Panel..."

I think Normal Effects will be fine but if not don't be afraid to enable more effects, you'll be fine.

It is very light on resources, I only have a 900MHz single processor, 1GB RAM and it works fine.

**Ubuntu menu as one icon instead of Apps/Places/System:**
Right-click panel, select "Add to Panel...", choose Main Menu, then Add.
To remove Apps/Places/System just right click it and Remove from Panel.

You have more than enough cpu/ram etc for all of this.

good luck

---

I recently broke up with my girlfriend of 5 years, for reasons unknown really - I just got to a point where I got scared it was too serious I guess. Problem is I think I still may love her. What does this have to do with James Spader's Alan Shore you ask? Well, I got addicted to watching TV series as a method of distracting myself from all the real issues in life and immersed myself in the wonderful world that was Boston Legal, sorta developed an obsession with Alan Shore (my favourite character) and I admire James Spaders performance. I nearly had John Hamm's, Don Draper, but this flirtatious and articulate lawyer won out.

### Post by armageddon08 on 2010-09-15
> **Islington said:**
> Nice. I think you, me and stanca are the only persistent kde posters anymore.  Btw how did you get minitunes to just show icons in the play toolbar?

Thanks! Yup, people seem to have been swayed by the light-themes/elementary and Faenza revolution ;).

In System Settings go to Fine Tuning under Style in Appearance and change Toolbars->Main toolbar text to "No Text".

### Post by Half-Left on 2010-09-16
> **labinnsw said:**
> The capability to do stuff like this is what I am waiting on to make the switch to Gnome Shell.

It is a while since I did a search, but I could not find any tutorials last time. Could you please point us to some info or knock up a little "How to?"

Well, because GNOME Shell is not finished, there is no tutorials on themes and the way GNOME Shell looks will probably change soon.

I learned myself but CSS is pretty easy and it's just a matter of knowing what themes what in the gnome-shell.css.

**Thanks for the comments from various people on the theme**. I'll let you guys know when I've released it. :)

**EDIT: **I probably should consider writing a small tutorial on how to theme the current GNOME Shell and some CSS tips in the tutorial & Tips part of the forum.

### Post by ljrmorgan on 2010-09-16
Here's my desktop.

I wonder if anyone can help me out with something - I gave openbox a try on my netbook and liked it, the only problem is that I want to use gnome too sometimes, at least until I get more used to OB. Thanks!

### Post by Tadcrazio on 2010-09-16

---

### Post by Tibuda on 2010-09-16
> **ljrmorgan said:**
> Here's my desktop.

I wonder if anyone can help me out with something - I gave openbox a try on my netbook and liked it, the only problem is that I want to use gnome too sometimes, at least until I get more used to OB. Gnome now looks crazy because I changed the gtk theme for OB - is there a way to get them to use different settings? I've had a quick google, but I couldn't find anything that sounded very promising. Thanks!

Yes. Just disable "gnome-settings-daemon" from running in Openbox, and set a ~/.gtkrc-2.0 file. Gnome will use the them settings from gconf and Openbox from the file.

To edit the ~/.gtkrc-2.0 file from a GUI, you could try lxappearance.

---

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-09-19
> **Shpongle said:**
> yea I know you can do this ,but it changes the docky dot and icon to red when I do that and that looks even more out of place , anybody have a work around ?

Set your selection Hue to around 220, set the saturation to 1 and the brightness/value to something higher than 20. Then you will have grey selection in the GTK, but blue dots on docky.

### Post by Half-Left on 2010-09-19
> **HeadHunter00 said:**
> hey half-life, how'd you install gnome shell in lucid? i cant seem to install it neither from the repositories nor the source code.if i install it from the repos, i get an error that libgjs0 cant be installed, when i install it from source code, it stops at the 20th step and asks me to retry it and etc. etc.

It's not very good for Lucid and Git it is pretty nasty at the moment. I personally recommend the one that comes with Maverick , which is GNOME Shell 2.31.5, which is before all of the major GTK breakage began and performance issues.

Maverick has Xorg 1.9 which is better for GNOME Shell. NVIDIA submitted a patch for Xorg which fixes performance issues, but I'm not sure if it will get into Maverick in time(it's currently in Xorg Git).

---

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-09-23
@ljrmorgan
 I thought your question was related to the screenshot you quoted, not what I use in OB in general.
 
 Anyways, my preferences;
 
 File Manager = Midnight Commander and Thunar
 Nothing beats MC, imho. For GUI, Thunar's a bit heavier than PCmanFM, but much more reliable in my experience (themes better as well)
 
 Terminal = Rxvt, Terminator 
 In most cases, rxvt (or one of it's variants like urxvt or mrxvt) running Screen (if you're familiar with it and can tolerate it's asinine idiosyncrasies) are all you'll need. Terminator I like because I can easily dedicate a workspace to a fullscreen session and have my favourite CLI apps 'tiled' in split mode [like this]("http://img826.imageshack.us/img826/3913/201009230945261600x900s.png"). The latest bzr version is pretty sweet, if a bit heavy and unstable.

Panel = tint2
You don't really need a panel in OB, but tint2 is probably the best choice if you want one. bmpanel is supposed to be good as well, but I haven't used it much. Avoid LXterminal like the plague (it's the fugliest thing in the universe!!)

Docks = F*ck No!!
Try AdeskBar if you want some form of pseudo-dock/launcher functionality. Mark can probably tell you more about it, since he's sort of the unofficial spokesperson/groupie/mascot. =P
 
 Editor = Vim, Nano, MCedit, Leafpad
 No explanation needed, really. If you want a GUI based one that's more feature-rich compared to Leafpad, there's Gedit, Geany and Mousepad
 
 Audio = MoC, MPD, CPlay, DeaDBeeF
 Purely personal, and there are way to many out there I have yet to try. I tend to prefer term based ones, but DeaDBeeF is the best GUI one for me. Note: My choices are based purely on audio quality. Playlist sorting features, Last.FM squabbling/wiggling and glitzy visualizers aren't my thing.
 
 Video = Mplayer (console) or Gnome-Mplayer (GUI)
 Nuff said.... the GUI frontend is actually pretty light, despite having the word 'Gnome' in it's name. 
 
 Browser = Midori, Opera, Uzbl, Elinks
 Again, it's personal preference. These are lighter than the usual Firefox and Chromium.

Others = dmenu (never leave home without it) , bashrun or gmrun (run dialogue), Pidgin or Centerim (IM client) , Irssi (IRC client)  Mutt, Alpine, Clawsmail (Email client),  Wicd or wicd-curses or ceni (lighter network-manager alternatives), xfce4-power-manager (works better and is lighter than the gnome one)

Just shoot a PM to any one of the OB users here and I'm sure they'll be able to help. You can also visit the CrunchBang, Gentoo or Arch forums for further info.

Cheers.

---

### Post by Mark76 on 2010-09-23
JP.

Have you tried ROX-Filer in session mode? (rox -S). That'll give you desktop wallpaper, iconised windows and launchers (.desktop files dragged and dropped on the pinboard).

Just remember to set "Pass all backdrop mouse clicks to window manager" to on.

### Post by ljrmorgan on 2010-09-24
> **HeadHunter00 said:**
> I know how to enable it but when i try installing it, it gives me an error than my glib version is too old. now, i cant really update glib without messing up the system now can i.

yeh, hence why it wont work in Lucid - I wouldn't recommend trying to update your whole system from some dodgy PPAs just to try and get Clutterflow working in nautilus elementary! (Incidentally it works for me now, it was a clutter problem, not nautilus elementary).

Anyway - you asked about Maverick. I'm using it on my desktop and my netbook. On my netbook a few things that worked in Lucid don't now work in Maverick (keeping track of battery life remaining being the most notable/irritating one). Everything works on my desktop, though I had to use the Xorg edgers PPA because compiz was glitchy - that fixed it though. That's just me though - you might find that nothing works properly on your system.

If I were you I wouldn't try it unless you're reasonably comfortable with the idea that everything might break - you don't want to upgrade to a testing version just to get the new (and not very good) sound indicator and then end up with a hosed system. That said, I've been trying alpha & beta releases for years just to try out the new features, and nothing has broken badly yet.

---

Hope the alcohol was good, None of that bland 'Mugi to Hoppu' stuff!! :P
Madras is such a cool name, don't know why they changed it to something else (starts with C, can't remember... maybe it sounds better to the locals). 
 

Yeah, I wasn't sure on what ScrotWM could or could not do. Good luck with the hacking, and hopefully you'll get something out of it. Thanks for introducing me to ScrotWM. Can't believe how easy everything was when I first started using it, from piping conky to the bar (I was never a big dzen fan) to defaults that didn't make me you go 'why the f*ck do I need to learn a new language just to set a wallpaper?!'. ScrotWM definitely deserves more love than it's getting (at least in the Linux world, it's probably more respected in BSD-land, I assume.... maybe it's the name O_o?)

The timing of your suggestions are pretty impeccable as well, considering I just reinstalled Death-to-the-Rat WM on one of my rigs a few minutes ago. Was about to dig up my old configs when I read your reply, so now I'll just wait for your PM instead :D

Cheers.

[LIST]
[*]CPU core 1

[*]Master volume
[*]seconds (just a filler, till I find something better :P)
[*]filesystem usage
[*]CPU core 2
[/LIST]

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-09-25
> **crl0901 said:**
> So sick.  I might need a tutorial on how to install and configure everything, looks complicated.

Thanks! 

It shouldn't be too complicated. I might write a script to install everything. In the meantime...

INSTALLATION:
Contents of theme.tar go in /usr/share/themes/
or you can just drag the individual folders (extract them first) into the appearance window [This will put them in ~/.themes/]

Contents of icons.tar go in /usr/share/icons/
or you can just drag the folder (extract it first) into the appearance window [This will put them in ~/.icons/]

Contents of extras.tar has the emerald theme and AWN theme. 
>> Open Emerald Themer, click "Import..." and choose the emerald theme. Run "emerald --replace"
>> Open AWN Dock Preferences, goto Themes, click "Install..." and choose the AWN theme.


DEPENDENCIES:
>> Nautilus Elementary for Breadcrumbs
sudo add-apt-repository ppa:am-monkeyd/nautilus-elementary-ppa
sudo apt-get update 
sudo apt-get upgrade
nautilus -q #restarts nautilus

Then open nautilus goto Edit > Preferences > Tweaks
and turn on breadcrumbs.
(You might have to quit it and open it again).


>> Equinox GTK Engine
sudo add-apt-repository ppa:tiheum/equinox
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get install gtk2-engines-equinox


>> AwOken icon set
sudo add-apt-repository ppa:alecive/antigone  
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get install awoken-icon-theme


>> AWN Lucido
Follow instructions [here...]("http://www.webupd8.org/2010/06/awn-lucido-gets-its-own-ppa.html")


I'm also using covergloobus with twquet theme and the screenlets clock.

### Post by Spike-X on 2010-09-25
> **Pablo Pablovski said:**
> Hey, any chance you could post your conkyrc? Liking the layout. :)

Thx..

No worries, here ya go! It took me freakin' HOURS to get this just right.

```
# UBUNTU-CONKY
# A comprehensive conky script, configured for use on
# Ubuntu / Debian Gnome, without the need for any external scripts.
#
# Based on conky-jc and the default .conkyrc.
# INCLUDES:
# - tail of /var/log/messages
# .conkyrc by Deguello

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes
xftfont AntiqueOliveStd-Bold:size=11
xftalpha 0.8
text_buffer_size 2048

# colours
color1 dark grey

color2 6892C6
# light blue

color3 3F3327
# brown

color4 dark grey
# gold

color5 CC0000
# red

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window no
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type widget
#own_window_type override
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

#background_yes

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 1920 50
maximum_width 1920

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 0

# border margins
border_margin 3

# border width
border_width 1

#lua_load ~/scripts/draw_bg.lua
#lua_draw_hook_pre draw_bg

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color black
default_shade_color dark grey
#default_outline_color grey
own_window_colour dark grey

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
alignment top_left
#alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 00
gap_y 00

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 2

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 2

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale yes

# Add spaces to keep things from moving about? This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer none

TEXT
#${image ~/fondo-mas-claro.png -p 0,0 -s 1920x50}
${color4}${voffset 5}${font StyleBats:size=16}A${font}  ${voffset -3}${color4}CPU1: ${color1}${cpu cpu1}% ${color4}${goto 110}${cpubar cpu1 10,60}${goto 200}${voffset -3}${color4}${font StyleBats:size=16}A${font}${voffset -3}${color4}  CPU3: ${color1}${cpu cpu3}% ${color4}${goto 310}${cpubar cpu3 10,60}${goto 400}${color4}${voffset -3}${font StyleBats:size=16}g${font}  ${voffset -3}${color4}RAM: ${color1}$memperc% ${color4}${goto 520}${membar 10,60}${goto 620}${color4}${voffset -3}${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=14}O${font}  ${color4}UP: ${color1}${upspeed eth1} kb/s ${color4}${goto 790}${upspeedgraph eth1 10,60 BEBEBE BEBEBE}${font}${goto 900}${color4}${voffset -2}${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=14}N${font}  ${color4}UPLOADED: ${color1}${goto 1050}${totalup eth1}${goto 1250}${execp conkyGuayadeque -n --template=~/conkyGuayadeque_ti.template} ${goto 1550}${voffset -17}${execp conkyGuayadeque -n --template=~/conkyGuayadeque_al.template}
${voffset -30}${color4}${font StyleBats:size=16}A${font}  ${voffset -3}${color4}CPU2: ${color1}${cpu cpu2}% ${color4}${goto 110}${cpubar cpu2 10,60}${goto 200}${voffset -3}${color4}${font StyleBats:size=16}A${font}  ${voffset -3}${color4}CPU4: ${font Agenda Light:size=10}${color1}${cpu cpu4}% ${color4}${goto 310}${cpubar cpu4 10,60}${font}${goto 400}${voffset -3}${color4}${font StyleBats:size=16}p${font}  ${voffset -4}${color4}UPTIME: ${color1}${goto 520}${uptime}${goto 620}${color4}${voffset -2}${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=14}U${font}  ${voffset -1}${color4}DOWN: ${color1}${downspeed eth1} kb/s ${color4}${goto 790}${downspeedgraph eth1 10,60 BEBEBE BEBEBE}${goto 900}${color4}${voffset -2}${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=14}T${font}  ${color4}DOWNLOADED: ${color1}${goto 1050}${totaldown eth1}${goto 1250}${execp conkyGuayadeque -n --template=~/conkyGuayadeque_ar.template}${goto 1550}${voffset -17}${execp conkyGuayadeque -n --template=~/conkyGuayadeque_yr.template}






```

(Sorry, couldn't get it to attach as a text file for some reason. The attachment manager just kept picking files at random, it seemed like)

Also, does anybody know how I can indent the notify pane thingy a little to the left so it doesn't overlap AWN?

### Post by 1991sudarshan on 2010-09-26
> **koleoptero said:**
> It's September somewhere already.

Rules:

1. Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
2. If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
3. Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
4. The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
5. The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
6. Please use reduced-size thumbnails, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
7. To avoid having users having to ask you for them. when possible we request that you format your posts in the following order: NOTE this is optional

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

**Important Note:** Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.


Here it goes:

GTK: Modified version of jurialmunkey's [Victorious Elements]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=9683935&postcount=208").
Metacity: The one included in the Absolute gtk theme (gnome-look.org)
Icons: Faenza Cupertino (gnome-look.org)
Wallpaper: [clicky]("http://dl.dropbox.com/u/1612038/1-9-10/2005-05-29-1920x1200.jpg")

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-09-27
> **slackthumbz said:**

I doubt it is the problem, but what version of Murrine do you have? I have Murrine 0.91. But that really shouldn't be the issue.

How did you install the themes?

Try installing the latest version that was uploaded today. Completely remove the themes then reinstall.

The only other thing I can think of is an ownership/permissions issue, but it looks like you already tried that.

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-09-27
> **slackthumbz said:**
> A quick run of apt-cache show gtk2-engines-murrine says I've got version 0.90.3+git20100323-0ubuntu3

I downloaded the 7zip archive from deviantart and ran the install script (after reading it first, I'm a little paranoid ;))

Always good practice to read scripts before running them. Its only there to simplify and streamline the whole process. I really cant think of what the problem is... you could try updating to a newer version of the murrine engine. 

I tried a fresh install, downloaded from DeviantArt and using the script and it works perfectly for me. I've only ever seen this when it was either permissions or missing an engine (my equinox is 1.30, murrine 0.91.0+git20100912~ppa1~lucid1, and pixmap engine has been built into GTK for quite a while).

You could try chown and chgrp to root then chmod read/write permissions.

What about if you just untar the themes manually and drag the folders over to the appearance window to install them? Does that work?

I really don't know what else it could be.

---

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-09-27
> **slackthumbz said:**
> tried dragging and dropping into the appearance window and despite apparently installing ok the theme still doesn't work. 

What are the exact requirements engine wise for it?
I've got the latest equinox and the stable repository version of murrine, is there anything else that I need?

PS, thanks for taking the time to help me out :)

Not a problem. :)

EDIT: I uploaded a new version @DeviantArt which should work with murrine 0.90.3

I just downgraded to the version of Murrine you are using. It is that. I'll upload a version which plays nice shortly. In the meantime just replace the text of the gtkrc in /gtk-2.0/ with the following (this is for plain Divergence III):
```
##########################################
# DIVERGENCE III
# by jurialmunkey
##########################################


##########################################
# COLOR SCHEME	
##########################################
gtk_color_scheme	= "bg_color:#D6D6D6\nselected_bg_color:#3A3B3D\nbase_color:#FFFFFF"	# Background, base.
gtk_color_scheme	= "fg_color:#2E2E2E\nselected_fg_color:#FFFFFF\ntext_color:#2E2E2E"	# Foreground, text.
gtk_color_scheme	= "tooltip_bg_color:#1f1f1f\ntooltip_fg_color:#e0e0e0" 			# Tooltips.
gtk_color_scheme	= "link_color:#08c"							# Hyperlinks
gtk_color_scheme	= "frame_color:#33322F\ninactive_frame_color:#33322F"			# Fix for Chrome
gtk_color_scheme 	= "menutxt_color:#d6d6d6\nmenubar_color:#3c3b37"			# Menubar Color
gtk_color_scheme 	= "sidebar_color:#32312E\nsidebar_txt:#d6d6d6"				# Nautilus Sidebar Color

gtk-icon-sizes = "panel-menu=22,22:panel=22,22:gtk-button=16,16:gtk-large-toolbar=22,22"
gtk-button-images	= 0			# Disables icons in buttons
gtk-toolbar-style	= 0			# Disables text in toolbar
gtk-auto-mnemonic	= 1			# Disables ugly lines under menu items




##########################################
# DEFAULT STYLE
##########################################

style "default"
{
		
	fg[NORMAL]        = @fg_color
	fg[PRELIGHT]      = @fg_color
	fg[SELECTED]      = @selected_fg_color
	fg[ACTIVE]        = @fg_color
	fg[INSENSITIVE]   = darker (@bg_color)

	bg[NORMAL]        = @bg_color
	bg[PRELIGHT]      = shade (1.02, @bg_color)
	bg[SELECTED]	  = @selected_bg_color
	bg[INSENSITIVE]   = @bg_color
	bg[ACTIVE]        = shade (1.04, @bg_color)

	base[NORMAL]      = @base_color
	base[PRELIGHT]    = shade (0.95, @bg_color)
	base[ACTIVE]      = shade (0.92, @selected_bg_color)
	base[SELECTED]    = shade (0.93, @selected_bg_color)
	base[INSENSITIVE] = @bg_color

	text[NORMAL]      = @text_color
	text[PRELIGHT]    = @text_color
	text[ACTIVE]      = @selected_fg_color
	text[SELECTED]    = @selected_fg_color
	text[INSENSITIVE] = darker (@bg_color)


# TOOLBAR STYLE PROPERTIES
	GtkToolbar::button-relief=GTK_RELIEF_NONE 	
	# Indicated the relief to be drawn around a GtkButton. 
	# GTK_RELIEF_NORMAL	Draw a normal relief. 
	# GTK_RELIEF_HALF	A half relief. 
	# GTK_RELIEF_NONE	No relief.

	GtkToolbar::internal-padding=0
	

	# GtkToolbar::shadow-type=GTK_SHADOW_ETCHED_IN
	# GTK_SHADOW_NONE	No outline. 
	# GTK_SHADOW_IN		The outline is bevelled inwards. 
	# GTK_SHADOW_OUT	The outline is bevelled outwards like a button. 
	# GTK_SHADOW_ETCHED_IN	The outline has a sunken 3d appearance. 
	# GTK_SHADOW_ETCHED_OUT	The outline has a raised 3d appearance


# SCALE (slider) STYLE PROPERTIES
	GtkScale::slider-length=14
	GtkScale::slider-width=14

# SCROLLBAR STYLE PROPERTIES
	#GtkScrollbar::fixed-slider-length=0
	#GtkScrollbar::has-backward-stepper=1
	#GtkScrollbar::has-forward-stepper=1
	#GtkScrollbar::has-secondary-backward-stepper=1
	#GtkScrollbar::min-slider-length=40

	GtkScrolledWindow::scrollbar-spacing=0
	GtkScrolledWindow::scrollbars-within-bevel=0
	#GtkScrolledWindow::window-placement-set=0
	#GtkScrolledWindow::window-placement=GTK_CORNER_BOTTOM_RIGHT

	#GtkScrolledWindow::vscrollbar_policy=GTK_POLICY_NEVER

	#GtkRange::trough-border=2
	#GtkRange::slider-width=9
	#GtkRange::stepper-size=12
	#GtkRange::stepper_spacing=0


# FOR PIXMAP SCROLLBAR
  GtkRange::trough-border = 0
  GtkRange::slider-width = 13
  GtkRange::stepper-size = 13

  GtkScrollbar::min_slider_length = 30

  GtkScrollbar::has-backward-stepper 			= 1
  #GtkScrollbar::has-secondary-backward-stepper 	= 1
  GtkScrollbar::has-forward-stepper			= 1
  #GtkScrollbar::has-secondary-forward-stepper		= 0
  



# PROGRESSBAR STYLE PROPERTIES
	GtkProgressBar::min-horizontal-bar-height=18
	GtkProgressBar::min-vertical-bar-width=18


# COMBOBOX / ENTRYBOX STYLE PROPERTIES
	GtkComboBox::appears-as-list=0
	GtkEntry::inner-border={2,2,2,2}
	GtkEntry::state-hint=0
	GtkEntry::honors-transparent-bg-hint=1
	GtkEntry::progress-border={3,3,3,3}


# MENU STYLE PROPERTIES
	GtkMenu::horizontal-padding=0
	GtkMenu::vertical-padding=0
	#GtkMenu::horizontal-offset  = -2
	GtkMenuBar::internal-padding=1
	GtkMenuBar::window-dragging=1

	#GtkMenuItem::vertical-padding=5
#	GtkMenuItem::selected-shadow-type=GTK_SHADOW_ETCHED_IN


# MISC STYLE PROPERTIES
	GtkWidget::new-tooltip-style=1
	GtkWidget::focus-padding=0
	GtkImage::x-ayatana-indicator-dynamic=1
	GtkPaned::handle-size=4
	GtkTreeView::expander-size=14
	GtkTreeView::vertical-separator=0
	GtkExpander::expander-size=16

# BUTTON STYLE PROPERTIES
	GtkButton::default_border = { 0, 0, 0, 0 }
	#GtkButton::child-displacement-x=1
	#GtkButton::child-displacement-y=1
	#GtkButton::displace-focus=1


# TABBED STYLE PROPERTIES
	GtkNotebook::tab-overlap=4
	GtkNotebook::tab-curvature=2


# HTML STYLE PROPERTIES
	GnomeHRef		::link_color  				= @link_color		
	GtkHTML			::link-color				= @link_color
 	GtkIMHtmlr		::hyperlink-color 			= @link_color
	GtkIMHtml		::hyperlink-color			= @link_color
	GtkWidget		::link-color				= @link_color
	GtkWidget		::visited-link-color			= @text_color

	xthickness = 1
	ythickness = 1

# DEFAULT ENGINE
	engine "equinox"
	{
		curvature           = 4
	        menubarstyle        = 1 # 0 = flat, 1 = gradient
	        toolbarstyle        = 3 # 0 = flat, 1 = gradient, 2 = flat without border, 3 = gradient without border, 4 = flat with bottom border, 5 = gradient with bottom border
	        buttonstyle         = 0 # 0 = normal, 1 = glassy
	        menuitemstyle       = 0 # 0 = normal, 1 = glassy
	        listviewheaderstyle = 0 # 0 = normal, 1 = glassy
	        scrollbarstyle      = 1 # 0 = normal, 1 = glassy, 2 = normal with handles, 3 = glassy with handles
	        scalesliderstyle    = 0 # 0 = normal, 1 = glassy, 2 = normal with bullet
	        checkradiostyle     = 1 # 0 = normal, 1 = glassy
	        progressbarstyle    = 0 # 0 = normal, 1 = glassy
	        separatorstyle      = 0 # 0 = solid, 1 = gradient
	        animation           = TRUE # FALSE = disabled, TRUE = enabled
	        arrowsize           = 0.1 # controls combo_arrow circle size.  Diameter set by (11 + 2 * arrowsize)		


	}
}
style "wide" = "default" {
    xthickness = 2
    ythickness = 2
}

style "wider" = "default" {
    xthickness = 3
    ythickness = 3
}

style "widest" = "default" {
    xthickness = 4
    ythickness = 3
}

##########################################
# TOOLBARS	
##########################################
style "toolbar" = "wide"
{
  fg[NORMAL] 		= @menutxt_color			
  fg[ACTIVE] 		= @menutxt_color			
  fg[PRELIGHT] 		= @menutxt_color			
  fg[SELECTED] 		= @menutxt_color			
  fg[INSENSITIVE] 	= @menutxt_color			

  bg[NORMAL] 		= @menubar_color	
  bg[ACTIVE] 		= @menubar_color			
  bg[PRELIGHT] 		= @menubar_color
  bg[SELECTED] 		= @menubar_color				
  bg[INSENSITIVE] 	= @menubar_color					
	engine "equinox"
	{
		curvature           = 4
	}
}

##########################################
# RADIOCHECK	
##########################################
style "radiocheck" = "wide"
{
  fg[NORMAL] 		= @fg_color			
  fg[ACTIVE] 		= @fg_color			
  fg[PRELIGHT] 		= @fg_color			
  fg[SELECTED] 		= @fg_color
  fg[INSENSITIVE] 	= @fg_color			
}

##########################################
# BUTTON	
##########################################
style "button" = "wide"
{
	#ythickness=4
		bg[PRELIGHT]      	 = shade (0.95, mix (0.85, @bg_color, @selected_bg_color))
		bg[ACTIVE]      	 = shade (0.85, @bg_color)


	fg[NORMAL]        = @fg_color
	fg[PRELIGHT]      = @fg_color
	fg[SELECTED]      = @selected_fg_color
	fg[ACTIVE]        = @fg_color
	fg[INSENSITIVE]   = darker (@bg_color)
	text[NORMAL]      = @text_color
	text[PRELIGHT]    = @text_color
	text[ACTIVE]      = @selected_fg_color
	text[SELECTED]    = @selected_fg_color
	text[INSENSITIVE] = darker (@bg_color)

	engine "equinox"
	{
		curvature           = 4
	}
}
style "dark-button" = "wide"
{
	fg[NORMAL]		= @menutxt_color
	fg[PRELIGHT]		= @menutxt_color
	fg[ACTIVE]		= @menutxt_color
	fg[SELECTED]		= @menutxt_color
	fg[INSENSITIVE]		= @menutxt_color

	text[NORMAL]		= @menutxt_color
	text[PRELIGHT]		= @menutxt_color
	text[ACTIVE]		= @menutxt_color
	text[SELECTED]		= @menutxt_color
	text[INSENSITIVE]	= @menutxt_color

	bg[NORMAL] 		= @menubar_color
	bg[PRELIGHT] 		= shade(1.3, @menubar_color)
	bg[ACTIVE] 		= shade(0.9, @menubar_color)
	bg[SELECTED] 		= @menubar_color
	bg[INSENSITIVE] 	= @menubar_color

	base[NORMAL] 		= @menubar_color
	base[PRELIGHT] 		= @menubar_color
	base[ACTIVE] 		= @menubar_color
	base[SELECTED] 		= @menubar_color
	base[INSENSITIVE] 	= @menubar_color

	engine "equinox"
	{
		curvature           = 4
	}
}

##########################################
# PROGRESSBAR	
##########################################
style "progressbar" = "default"
{
	bg[SELECTED]	  = shade (0.90, mix (0.20, @bg_color, @sidebar_color))
	engine "equinox"
	{
		curvature           = 12
	}
}

##########################################
# ENTRYBOX	
##########################################
style "entrybox" = "wider"
{
	engine "murrine" {
		contrast = 0.6
		arrowstyle = 2
		reliefstyle = 3
		highlight_shade = 1.0
		glazestyle = 0
	#	default_button_color = shade (1.1, @selected_bg_color)
		gradient_shades = {1.1, 1.0, 1.0, 0.9}
		roundness = 4
		lightborder_shade = 1.26
		lightborderstyle = 1
		listviewstyle = 2
		progressbarstyle = 0
		colorize_scrollbar = FALSE
		menubaritemstyle = 1
		menubarstyle = 1
		menustyle = 2
	#	focusstyle = 3
	#	handlestyle = 1
		sliderstyle = 3
	#	handlestyle = 1
		scrollbarstyle = 2
		stepperstyle = 3
#		rgba = TRUE

		
	}
}
style "dark-entrybox" = "entrybox"
{

	text[NORMAL]      = @fg_color
	text[PRELIGHT]    = @fg_color
	text[ACTIVE]      = @selected_fg_color
	text[SELECTED]    = @selected_fg_color
	text[INSENSITIVE] = darker (@bg_color)
}
##########################################
# TOOLTIPS	
##########################################
style "tooltips" = "widest"
{

fg[NORMAL] 		= @selected_fg_color			# TEXT COLOR
bg[NORMAL] 		= @selected_bg_color		# BG COLOR
bg[SELECTED] 		= @selected_bg_color			# BORDER


engine "equinox" {curvature = 12}
}

##########################################
# NOTEBOOK (TABS)	
##########################################
style "notebook" = "default"
{
	bg[NORMAL]	= shade (1.05, @bg_color)	# selected tab entire
	bg[ACTIVE]	= shade (0.95, @bg_color)	# unselected tab
	engine "equinox"
	{
		curvature = 6
	}
}

##########################################
# MENUBAR
##########################################
style "menubar" = "default"
{
  xthickness=1
  ythickness=2

  fg[NORMAL]   		= @menutxt_color	# MENUBAR TEXT COLOR
  bg[NORMAL]   		= @menubar_color	# MENUBAR BG COLOR
  fg[PRELIGHT] 		= @menutxt_color	# SELECTED MENUBAR TEXT
  bg[SELECTED] 		= @menubar_color	# SELECTED MENUBAR BUTTON

  fg[SELECTED] 		= @menutxt_color
  bg[PRELIGHT]		= @menubar_color
  fg[ACTIVE]		= "#808080"
  fg[INSENSITIVE]	= "#808080"

  text[NORMAL] 		= @menutxt_color
  text[PRELIGHT] 	= @menutxt_color
  text[SELECTED] 	= @menutxt_color
  text[ACTIVE] 		= "#808080"
  text[INSENSITIVE] 	= "#808080"
}

##########################################
# MENUS	
##########################################
style "lightmenuitem" = "wider"
{
  xthickness=0
  fg[NORMAL] 		= @menubar_color
  bg[NORMAL] 		= @menutxt_color
  fg[PRELIGHT] 		= @selected_fg_color
  bg[SELECTED] 		= shade (1.0, @menubar_color)

  bg[PRELIGHT] 		= shade (1.0, @menubar_color)
  fg[SELECTED] 		= shade (1.0, @menutxt_color)
  fg[ACTIVE] 		= "#808080"
  fg[INSENSITIVE] 	= "#808080"

  text[NORMAL] 		= @menutxt_color
  text[PRELIGHT] 	= @menutxt_color
  text[SELECTED] 	= @menutxt_color
  text[ACTIVE] 		= "#808080"
  text[INSENSITIVE] 	= "#808080"

engine "equinox" {curvature = 4}

}
style "lightmenu" = "default"
{
  xthickness=0
  ythickness=3

  fg[NORMAL] 		= @menutxt_color			# MENU TEXT COLOR
  bg[NORMAL] 		= shade (1.0, @menubar_color)		# MENU BG COLOR
  fg[PRELIGHT] 		= @selected_fg_color			# SELECTED TEXT COLOR
  bg[SELECTED] 		= @selected_bg_color			# SELECTION BOX
  bg[ACTIVE] 		= shade (1.0, @menubar_color)		# MENU BORDER COLOR

  bg[PRELIGHT] 		= @selected_bg_color
  fg[SELECTED] 		= @selected_bg_color
  fg[ACTIVE] 		= "#808080"
  fg[INSENSITIVE] 	= "#808080"

  text[NORMAL] 		= @menutxt_color
  text[PRELIGHT] 	= @menutxt_color
  text[SELECTED] 	= @menutxt_color
  text[ACTIVE] 		= "#808080"
  text[INSENSITIVE] 	= "#808080"

	engine "murrine" {
		contrast = 0.6
		arrowstyle = 2
		reliefstyle = 3
		highlight_shade = 1.0
		glazestyle = 1
		glowstyle = 0
		glow_shade = 1.7
	#	default_button_color = shade (1.0, @menubar_color)
		gradient_shades = {1.3, 1.2, 1.1, 1.0}
		roundness = 0
		lightborder_shade = 1.7
		lightborderstyle = 1
		listviewstyle = 2
		menubaritemstyle = 1
		menubarstyle = 1
		menustyle = 2
		stepperstyle = 3
}
}

##########################################
# EXTRAS	
##########################################
style "infobar" {
	engine "murrine" {
		roundness = 6
		border_shades = {1.16, 1.0}
		glow_shade = 1.1
		glowstyle = 5
	
}
}

style "iconview" {
	engine "murrine" {
		roundness = 6
		border_shades = {1.16, 1.0}
		glow_shade = 1.1
		glowstyle = 5
	}
}

# FIX EVOLUTION NEW BUTTON
style "evo_new_button_workaround" {
  fg[NORMAL] 		= @menutxt_color			
  fg[ACTIVE] 		= @menutxt_color			
  fg[PRELIGHT] 		= @menutxt_color			
  fg[SELECTED] 		= @menutxt_color			

  bg[NORMAL] 		= @menubar_color	
  bg[ACTIVE] 		= @menubar_color			
  bg[PRELIGHT] 		= @menubar_color
  bg[SELECTED] 		= @menubar_color
}
##########################################
# MATCHES	
##########################################
class "GtkWidget"    				style "default"

class "GtkRange"     				style "wide"
class "GtkFrame"     				style "widest"
class "GtkSeparator" 				style "wide"

class "GtkInfoBar" 				style "infobar"
class "GtkIconView" 				style "iconview"

widget_class "*.<GtkButton>*"   		style "button"
widget_class "*Gedit*.<GtkButton>*"   		style "button"
widget_class "*.<GtkRadioButton>*"                       	style "radiocheck"
widget_class "*.<GtkCheckButton>*"                         	style "radiocheck"

widget_class "*.<GtkOptionMenu>*"         	style "button"
widget_class "*.<GtkScaleButton>*"         	style "button"
widget_class "*.<GtkVolumeButton>*"         	style "button"
widget_class "*.<GtkLinkButton>*"         	style "button"
widget_class "*.<GtkColorButton>*"         	style "button"
widget_class "*.<GtkFontButton>*"         	style "button"

widget_class "*<GtkCombo>*"         		style "entrybox"
widget_class "*<GtkEntry>*"         		style "entrybox"
widget_class "*<GtkComboBox>*"         		style "entrybox"
widget_class "*<GtkComboBoxEntry>*"		style "entrybox"

widget_class "*<GtkNotebook>*<GtkEventBox>"     style "notebook"
widget_class "*<GtkNotebook>*<GtkDrawingArea>"  style "notebook"
widget_class "*<GtkNotebook>*<GtkLayout>"       style "notebook"
widget_class "*<GtkNotebook>*<GtkLabel>"	style "notebook"
widget_class "*<GtkNotebook>"    		style "notebook"

widget_class "*<GtkProgress>"			style "progressbar"
widget_class "*<GtkProgressBar>"       		style "progressbar"

widget_class "EShellWindow.GtkVBox.BonoboDock.BonoboDockBand.BonoboDockItem*" style "evo_new_button_workaround"

widget "gtk-tooltip*" 				style "tooltips"

##########################################
# PIXMAP ADDITIONS #######################
##########################################
###### TOOLBAR ###########################
##########################################
style "toolbar-pix"
{
	engine "pixmap"
	{
		image
		{
			function	= BOX
			file		= "Toolbar/toolbar.png"
			border	= { 8, 8, 8, 8}
			stretch	= TRUE
    		}
 	}
}
widget_class "*BonoboDockItem" style "toolbar"
class "*BonoboDockItem" style "toolbar"

widget_class "*HandleBox" style "toolbar"
class "*HandleBox" style "toolbar"

widget_class "*Toolbar" style "toolbar"
class "*Toolbar" style "toolbar"

##########################################
### MENU #################################
##########################################
style "menu-pix"			= "default"
{
xthickness			= 3
ythickness			= 1

  fg[NORMAL]   		= @menutxt_color	# MENUBAR TEXT COLOR
  bg[NORMAL]   		= @menubar_color	# MENUBAR BG COLOR
  fg[PRELIGHT] 		= @menutxt_color	# SELECTED MENUBAR TEXT
  bg[SELECTED] 		= @menubar_color	# SELECTED MENUBAR BUTTON

  fg[SELECTED] 		= @menutxt_color
  bg[PRELIGHT]		= @menubar_color
  fg[ACTIVE]		= "#808080"
  fg[INSENSITIVE]	= "#808080"

  text[NORMAL] 		= @menutxt_color
  text[PRELIGHT] 	= @menutxt_color
  text[SELECTED] 	= @menutxt_color
  text[ACTIVE] 		= "#808080"
  text[INSENSITIVE] 	= "#808080"

engine "pixmap"
	{
		image
		{
			function	= BOX
			state = NORMAL
			file		= "Toolbar/menubar.png"
			border	= { 8, 8, 8, 8}
			stretch	= TRUE
    		}

		image
		{
			function	= BOX
			state = ACTIVE
			file		= "Toolbar/menubar.png"
			border	= { 0, 0, 0, 0 }
			stretch	= TRUE
    		}

		image
		{
			function	= BOX
			state = INSENSITIVE
			file		= "Toolbar/menubar.png"
			border	= { 0, 0, 0, 0 }
			stretch	= TRUE
    		}
		
			
}
}
class "GtkMenuBar*" 		     	style "menu-pix"
widget_class "*MenuBar.*"  		style "menu-pix"

widget_class "*<GtkMenuItem>"		style "lightmenuitem"
class "GtkMenuItem"           		style "lightmenuitem"
class "GtkTearoffMenuItem"		style "lightmenuitem"

class "GtkMenu"       			style "lightmenu"
widget_class "*<GtkMenu>*"              style "lightmenu"

##########################################
# INCLUDES	
##########################################
include "Styles/nautilus.rc"
include "Styles/panel.rc"
include "Styles/scrollbar.rc"

widget_class "*<GtkToolbar>*<GtkButton>*"     	style "toolbar"

include "Styles/breadcrumbs.rc"


```

### Post by mrdiego on 2010-09-29
> **sendblink23 said:**
> Where did you get GimpBox ? I want my Gimp to be that way in a box =P

One bug is that you can't open in a "gimpbox" via Nautilus your images. ;)

cheers

### Post by Half-Left on 2010-09-30
> **deewatsa said:**
> Very nice, I have not tried GS yet but what is used for compositing?

Mutter is the window manager, which replaces metacity. GNOME Shell only works with compositing.

### Post by mrdiego on 2010-09-30
> 1. Can u disable "Recent Items"?
> 1. No (though not sure if you could in the javascript parts).

This is a great pitty, because not everybody wish it. For somebodies seems to be a great feature, for others a big handycap or even a limitation in freedom ... for example if I don't want show what files I watched recently - to anybody; not in my work, in family, even in public Screenshots. "Unity" haves the same trouble... "Recent Items" should have a option for disable, hide or be "manage-able". At moment it's a Bug which catchs or limits the freedom in human actions for me. It's my opinion... But maybe I am wrong!? I know only that I won't have Unity or Gnome Shell running on my PC for that reason. :/ (sadly but true - Metallica)
